<span id="freeTextContainer5592697866650222846">First off let me thank my Floridian alter ego (my goodreads friend Page Turner ) for loaning me this mind fuck. <br/><br/>Well, if you are in the mood for a mind fuck of the Consequences series variety, this is the book for you! It's part one of two, ends on a cliffy but second book due out later this month. <br/><br/>I couldn't stand the H in this book. Just asshole. <br/>The h was annoying.   <span id="freeText5592697866650222846" style="display:none">First off let me thank my Floridian alter ego (my goodreads friend Page Turner ) for loaning me this mind fuck. <br /><br />Well, if you are in the mood for a mind fuck of the Consequences series variety, this is the book for you! It's part one of two, ends on a cliffy but second book due out later this month. <br /><br />I couldn't stand the H in this book. Just asshole. <br />The h was annoying. Every time this asshole swung his dick her way she was sucking it. <br /><br />Our little h has amnesia after a car accident and remembers nothing about her life with asshole and their two badly behaved girls , who she loves anyway. So if amnesia storyline irks you, skip this. <br /><br />The prologue gives away much of the storyline. You may want to skip it and read it after ( makes it more fun). I found the story itself was entertaining despite not liking this couple. Some of my friends on here five starred it. <br /><br />Enjoy! <br /><br />Side note. One weird thing. The author promotes one of her books, within this book. No kidding. You will laugh when you read that part. So cheesy. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398828888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1042015299377472269"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409952605i/11045361.png' width='400' height='40' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Title:</b> Suit<br/><b>Series:</b> (Twin Duo, #1)<br/><b>Author:</b> <br/><b>Genre</b>: Dark Romantic Suspense<br/><b>Rating:</b> 5-Stars<br/><b>Cliffhanger:</b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[OMFG YES! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><b>HEA:</b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[No. *crosses fingers and hopes for an HEA in book #2* <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><b>Review on Blog:</b> <a href='http://thisjabberwockyeatsbooks.blogspot.com/2015/10/favorite-book-review-twin-duo-1-suit-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409952682i/11045378.png' width='400' height='40' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>There were no visions of a past, no recollections of who I was or where I had come from. Nothing but unconscious darkness.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Waking up from a coma with a broken body and scarred mind, <b>Gabriella Pierce is forced to live a life she doesn't remem</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1042015299377472269" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409952605i/11045361.png" width="400" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Title:</b> Suit<br><b>Series:</b> (Twin Duo, #1)<br><b>Author:</b> <br><b>Genre</b>: Dark Romantic Suspense<br><b>Rating:</b> 5-Stars<br><b>Cliffhanger:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OMFG YES! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. *crosses fingers and hopes for an HEA in book #2* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Review on Blog:</b> <a href="http://thisjabberwockyeatsbooks.blogspot.com/2015/10/favorite-book-review-twin-duo-1-suit-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409952682i/11045378.png" width="400" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>There were no visions of a past, no recollections of who I was or where I had come from. Nothing but unconscious darkness.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Waking up from a coma with a broken body and scarred mind, <b>Gabriella Pierce is forced to live a life she doesn't remember</b>. Who is this man who <b>holds her hand <i>too</i> tight</b>, who glares at her with contempt? Who are the two little adorable little girls who call her 'Mommy'? <br><br><b>Who do these memories</b>—these bits and pieces of the puzzle her mind has become—<b>belong to?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426793134ra/14097178.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Because what she feels and remembers, isn't what they tell her</b>—isn't what he tells her: her husband, Paxton Pierce, the man who takes everything and gives nothing. <b>The man who'll yank her hair, spank her bottom, who'll tenderly kiss her lips goodbye.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Paxton spun me, slamming my hands hard against the door. His body molded with mine and I pressed my naked back into his chest. My heart beat in my ears as my body surrender to pure ecstasy. Paxton Pierce was my drug of choice. Pure, exotic, ecstasy.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>And as Gabriella's mind heals from the accident, her mind doesn't. Days and weeks pass, as <b>she's trapped with a man she hates to love, with a man that loves to hate her</b>. But with each different, <i>wrong</i> piece of her, with each punishing grip, angry fuck, whispered, kiss-worthy confession, <b>Paxton and Gabriella fall into a dark, deep love all over again.</b><br><br>Only, it feels like the first time—but it isn't, is it? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395256144ra/8972750.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Being inside the mind of Gabriella was a terribly, lovely experience. Even though she never knew who or where she belonged, she still had a fire and a passion about her that I admired. She was strong, even when she seemed weak; even when she was forced to submit—eyes lowered, and knees trembling...thriving on Paxton's punishments, on his selfish nature.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Paxton and his power trip degraded me with elegance like it was his honorably duty to disgrace me with dignity.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Ugh. Paxton. Pax. My wicked, wacky love. <b>He enraged me, he captivated me.</b> One moment I loathed him, the next I loved him—just as one page he was mean, controlling, cruel, and the next he was soft, tender, gentle enough to make me forgive all his sins.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445478583ra/16656851.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From the first chapter—<i>the first chapter</i>—I was utterly and completely intrigued in this story. Everything about it appealed to me: <b>the mystery, the rough-love, the deep-rooted hate, the nail-biting suspense, the mind-bogging characters, the tiniest, spark of hope...</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The pit of my stomach balled and tightened. A gut feeling. That dreaded instinct when you know you’re doing something wrong, or you can sense something bad about to happen.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>...that quickly died, as my hopes were drenched with tears on the last page when I realized all my questions, all my answers, were only the beautiful, shocking beginning.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416419ra/822369.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You have everything to suit your needs, and I have you. My slut, to suit mine.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><b><i>Suit (The Twin Duo, #1)</i> will entice you, it'll deprive you, it'll keep you gasping for more</b>—as Paxton's hand was wrapped like a pretty bow around your throat...punishing you, pleasing you, for wanting more.<br><br><b>AS <u>AMAZING</u> AS ALICE'S DREAMS:</b> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444795485i/16554268.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443478323i/16364197.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1394684091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394684091" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21044214-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373736739p2/21044214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394684091?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/21044214-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394684091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223281294643685212">Full review here => <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://afterdarkbooklovers.com/2015/09/29/blog-tour-book-review-suit-by-jettie-woodruff/'>http://afterdarkbooklovers.com/2015/0...</a><br/><br/>As a blogger, we get a lot of email requests to review new releases. As a reader, I'm always searching for that special book, something that will draw me from the first page and make me want to scream from the rooftops on how good it is, once I'm done. The synopsis for this book caught my attention, so I requested it as it looked like some mink fuckery would be in store. I'm always in the book for a good mind fuck, and this book deliver</span>
  <span id="freeText3223281294643685212" style="display:none">Full review here =&gt; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://afterdarkbooklovers.com/2015/09/29/blog-tour-book-review-suit-by-jettie-woodruff/">http://afterdarkbooklovers.com/2015/0...</a><br /><br />As a blogger, we get a lot of email requests to review new releases. As a reader, I'm always searching for that special book, something that will draw me from the first page and make me want to scream from the rooftops on how good it is, once I'm done. The synopsis for this book caught my attention, so I requested it as it looked like some mink fuckery would be in store. I'm always in the book for a good mind fuck, and this book delivered!<br /><br />The idea of twin sisters seemed very unique to me. Especially how the author wove a story around identity. Adding to the theme are the two covers. Did you notice how fucking brilliant they are? One is called Suit, one is called Slut. Did you look closely and see how the words are almost look identical? Maybe I'm reading to much into this (pun intended), but if this was intentional, I want to give the author a virtual high five. Seriously, so clever!<br /><br />If you read the synopsis, you are probably scratching your head like I was on what sort of story this might be about. 10% in and I'm already creating wild theories in my head as to what is going on. Which of course, I can't share with you. <br /><br />The pace of this story kept me engaged and constantly speculating. Following Gabriella's accident, I had my theory as to what happened. And I was convinced I was right until the very end. Now I don't know what to think. I wasn't sure which way is up. My brain hurt. This is one of those times when I am frustrated with ARCs because I have no one to talk to and speculate on what is going on.<br /><br />What I can tell you is that Gabriella's marriage to Paxton is all sorts of messed up. I'm not certain how the two of them came to be, you are given the sense that Paxton isn't in love with her, and has never been. Yet he can't seem to keep his hands off of her. You thought Christian Grey was a control freak? HA! Paxton now seems to define that term. To give you an example, he checks Gabriella's mileage before she leaves the hours, because she's only allowed to travel so far. SAY WHAT? And that's just the tip of the iceburg. He is a jackass to Gabriella for a good part of the book. But, he's not a complete dick. He's actually a great father and smart businessman.<br /><br /><i>“You have everything to suit your needs, and I have you. My slut, to suit mine.”</i><br /><br />What was most interesting about this couple was how they interacted privately. Paxton lobbies threats to Gabriella for backtalking, not following the rules, etc. He intitially punishes her by controlling her orgasms, teasing her to a point, but not taking her over the edge. What was even more interesting was how Gabriella's reactions threw him off. She got off on his domination. And this completely confused Paxton. <br /><br /><i>“This isn’t funny, Gabriella. I can’t even humiliate you with an ass beating anymore. Your pussy likes that, too. I don’t know what to do. This isn’t you.”</i><br /><br />You got the sense that prior to the accident, she was dry during every physical encounter. Now she gets turned on by the punishments. This changes the dynamics of their relationship in a big way. In a good way. And had me thinking my early theory was correct, even though I have no idea on the particulars of what happened.<br /><br />Throughout the book, Gabriella has flashback to her childhood with her Mom and twin sister Isabella. We learn the rough life she lived and how she and her sister eventually separate. But a lot of pieces are missing form the puzzle. It's not until the very end that the author gives us that huge corner piece, leaving me rewarded and at the same time, extremely confused. It's that cliffhanger you knew was coming. <br /><br />This is that book that makes me want to scream from the rooftops! This is something book clubs should read (kinky ones, of course), because this story is one you want to talk out. I’m dying for others to read this and give me their thoughts. My theory is nearly confirmed but the author added huge twist, and there are so many other part of the story left unturned. I’ll be checking my kindle daily waiting for book 2, that is for sure.<br /><br />*An ARC was received for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_1450662925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1450662925" />
    <a title="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11672704-donna-the-romance-cover"><img alt="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369044455p2/11672704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1450662925?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" href="/user/show/11672704-donna-the-romance-cover">Donna ~ The Romance Cover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11672704-donna-the-romance-cover?shelf=4-5-star-reads-2015">4-5-star-reads-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1450662925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13797893542461875387">Suit (the Twin Duo #1)<br/>Slut (the Twin Duo #2) by Jettie Woodruff<br/>Suit 4.5 stars!! Slut 4 stars!!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was always the quiet one, the one who followed suit, doing what others told me to do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>This was one of those series that I knew I needed to read in one hit, I had heard the whispers on the grapevine and I was glad that I had decided to read them together. The first book had me on the edge of my seat frantically page turning. What a mind f@@k!! This book had my head all over the place but i</span>
  <span id="freeText13797893542461875387" style="display:none">Suit (the Twin Duo #1)<br />Slut (the Twin Duo #2) by Jettie Woodruff<br />Suit 4.5 stars!! Slut 4 stars!!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was always the quiet one, the one who followed suit, doing what others told me to do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />This was one of those series that I knew I needed to read in one hit, I had heard the whispers on the grapevine and I was glad that I had decided to read them together. The first book had me on the edge of my seat frantically page turning. What a mind f@@k!! This book had my head all over the place but in a really good way. An intricate storyline that will have you reading between the lines, assuming and then unassuming. Just when you think you know what is going on it isn’t and you are back to where you started…knowing nothing at all.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was the missing link, the broken one that didn’t fit anymore.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I have to admit that in the beginning Paxton was a tough cookie to like, he came across as an obnoxious asshole, dominating, possessive and a touch sadistic. He lacked emotion and empathy, he was an empty vessel. But, and this is a huge BUT, I knew that there must have been a different side to him.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You have everything to suit your needs, and I have you. My slut, to suit mine.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Paxton was an amazing father and when you saw him with his kids you just knew that there was a different man underneath the charade. Having had the benefit of reading book two as well I am glad that I was proven correct, but by the end of book two (Slut) I adored him, despite his domineering ways.<br /><br />Gabriella was Paxton’s wife and after a car accident she wakes up with amnesia. She doesn’t recognise her husband or her children and everything around her is alien and confusing. Gabriella struggles to fit back into her old life, especially with regards to Paxton and his emotionless ways. Everything seems to be a charade and she just wants to be Gabriella, but is the Gabriella that woke up the same Gabriella before the accident?<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I loved him, and I loved our magic. Even if it was all messed up. It was out and nothing could change that, until it could.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />With secrets and lies and little flickers of recollection slowly but surely coming through vivid dreams Gabriella thinks that she is slowly piecing together her life before and leading up to the accident that claimed her memory…or is it? Is everything as it seems?<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“No, tell me truth. I’ve heard enough lies for a lifetime.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Slut was not as intense as book one, Suit. Slut is what I call a book of revelations. A book where the past is finally revealed piece by little piece and secrets and truths are painfully divulged. Everything you thought you knew you don’t and what you thought was real was and wasn’t.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Change the way you look at things and the things you look at will change.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I loved how the past was revealed, I loved the transformation of Paxton and how we finally got to see the real him. For a man that I had loathed in the beginning I was glad my gut instinct had not let me down. He really puts himself out there in this book and I could understand why he was his emotionless self in Suit.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We’re the perfect storm of two kinds of crazy.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />This was a book of second chances, a redo, how not to repeat the mistakes of the past when you are given the chance of a clean slate and a fresh future. I loved it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“…I’m so stoked to make new memories.”<br />“I promise to make them better than the ones you forgot.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I understand a Novella will be released in December. For this I am thankful, I still have a few questions that I hope will get answered…I cannot wait!!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theromancecover.com">www.theromancecover.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13797893542461875387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1408781182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1408781182" />
    <a title="Naksed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed"><img alt="Naksed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417804998p2/29458352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1408781182?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naksed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naksed" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed">Naksed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=hero-is-a-big-fat-jerk">hero-is-a-big-fat-jerk</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1408781182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11708819827345689168">It was okay. Jettie Woodruff is using her formula of the abusive jerk and amnesiac heroine that worked very well in her Underestimated series, except she has added a couple of cute kids and a set of twins to the equation. I don't read this author's books for her impeccable spelling and grammar so all the editing errors did not bother me too much. I knew what I was getting into. I like her books because they are fast-paced, pulpy and OTT in a rather exhilarating way. Though I do think the suppose</span>
  <span id="freeText11708819827345689168" style="display:none">It was okay. Jettie Woodruff is using her formula of the abusive jerk and amnesiac heroine that worked very well in her Underestimated series, except she has added a couple of cute kids and a set of twins to the equation. I don't read this author's books for her impeccable spelling and grammar so all the editing errors did not bother me too much. I knew what I was getting into. I like her books because they are fast-paced, pulpy and OTT in a rather exhilarating way. Though I do think the supposed twist ending was predictable from a mile away, and her big fat jerk hero gross beyond repair. I also don't like it when authors promote themselves inside the fictional world they created. When the female protag gleefully downloads Jettie Woodruff's Black Rain on her tablet and immediately pre-orders the sequel, Midnight Rain, because it would make perfect vacation read, I really had to roll my eyes.<br /><br />The parts of the book that worked best for me, that came alive from the pages, and had real emotional depth and poignancy were the flashbacks to the main character's traumatic childhood, traipsing around the country with a mentally unstable, heroin-addicted mother, and a weak,needy sibling. I wonder if the author pushed herself to do it, whether she could pull off a literary fiction that focuses on the painful family dysfunction, childhood abuse, and the emotional bonds between parent and child, themes that she returns to again and again in her novels. The sincerity of her point of view, and the vivid images she creates, like the mother and her girls perched on a billboard while airplanes fly over, or when they embark on a four day trek as stowaways on a dusty train, made me ache to read more about them, and to follow these little girls on a journey where they could conquer the trauma, instability, and recklessness inflicted on them.<br /><br />I am not sure that I was sufficiently sucked in to this story to read the next volume. I do love this author's boldness in going "there" where few others dare to go, and I generally enjoy her books but this felt a bit like deja vu.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11708819827345689168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_23163343'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23163343-debt"><img alt="Debt" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1413361621l/23163343._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tk1OzR20IDPMbSc95p57ZbGJm8SYsP4XvYAhbHhF2oP+u86Vp5RC/zAXKf7i3DnAU58ehEM1F13Mwx8JXvEsiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
